  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c2b41f8e-adea-44bd-97d9-93f9f0a6265c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/498184-just-finished-reading-the-book-but-i-m">Just finished reading the book but I&#39;m still utterly confused about the difference between Carter magic and Free magic? Why is it that carter mages feel sick when they are near Free magic? I dont think there was a clear explanation of free magic and carter magic in the book but I might have missed it so if there&#39;s any kind soul that can explain it to me, it would be greatly appreciated!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_498184'><a id="like_count_community_question_498184" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/498184?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F518848.Sabriel">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/498184-just-finished-reading-the-book-but-i-m">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/498184-just-finished-reading-the-book-but-i-m">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1409961-maya"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1409961-maya">Maya</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Well, the history behind this explained more in the sequels, but essentially Free Magic in and of itself isn't necessarily "good" or "evil", it's just<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Well, the history behind this explained more in the sequels, but essentially Free Magic in and of itself isn't necessarily "good" or "evil", it's just pure power-and it's wielded by necromancers because I guess it's stronger, but also more unpredictable. Charter magic was created as a way to harness Free Magic into a more usable and safe method of performing magic--through symbols. I'm not necessarily sure if there's a ~reason~ per say that Free Magic makes mages sick, but it's likely to do with the fact that it's so strong that it has an adverse effect on the body. It's supposed to be almost corrosive, and that wielding it is detrimental to a person's health. Which is why necromancers resort to more and more extreme measures to stay alive. Hope I helped!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_953475'><a id="like_count_community_question_953475" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/953475?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F518848.Sabriel">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1404450006i/32761625._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32761625-cassandra">Cassandra</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes it does jump straight in, but if you just keep going the world-building happens as you go. In case you still want some info, basically the world i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes it does jump straight in, but if you just keep going the world-building happens as you go. In case you still want some info, basically the world is two parts - Ancelstierre, where Sabriel grows up, is like a late 19th century Britain - early electricity, guns, some cars, etc. The Old Kingdom, separated by a wall, is more mediævil and has magic and necromancy and cool stuff like that. Most of this book happens in the Old Kingdom. Hope that helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_104924126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104924126" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104924126?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of LOTR and Fantasy Genre</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=fun-fantasy">fun-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=australian-writer">australian-writer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104924126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9149832035301212414">I picked this book up from the library and noticed stickers on the book declaring that it was part of a reading challenge here in NSW for grades 7-8.<br/><br/>"This book is acceptable to read for 12-13 year olds? Fuck me, can we turn around and go back to the library?" I asked my husband.<br/><br/>He shook his head and smiled at me. "Just try it. You never know."<br/><br/>"It's for twelve-to-thirteen year olds! No sex! No swearing! Minimum violence! I don't fucking think so!"<br/><br/>In the end, we brought it home and I sulked the wh</span>
  <span id="freeText9149832035301212414" style="display:none">I picked this book up from the library and noticed stickers on the book declaring that it was part of a reading challenge here in NSW for grades 7-8.<br /><br />"This book is acceptable to read for 12-13 year olds? Fuck me, can we turn around and go back to the library?" I asked my husband.<br /><br />He shook his head and smiled at me. "Just try it. You never know."<br /><br />"It's for twelve-to-thirteen year olds! No sex! No swearing! Minimum violence! I don't fucking think so!"<br /><br />In the end, we brought it home and I sulked the whole way. However yesterday I opened it up and thought I'd actually give it a try and I'm really glad it did.<br /><br />It actually managed to have more romance in it than Darkfever did, and that bloody book has NAKED people on the front cover, for crying out loud!<br /><br />I thought this was going to be a story about a young girl on a magical adventure with a sword and a bad hair-do. But it turns out it's about an eighteen year old woman with dark, deadly skills being chased and hunted by a terrible and deadly enemy.<br /><br />Sabriel has a good, clear head on her shoulder. She's smart, she's strong, she's a well-balanced and interesting character. The characters in Sabriel are all interesting and capturing in their way. Mogget was just pure win. He cracked me up. Touchstone was annoying at first but quickly won me over.<br /><br />The world is interesting and complex, filled with enough creepy things that go bump in the night to really freak me out.<br /><br />That's the best thing about this book. It's not TRYING to be a children's book. The rising action, climax and VERY short denouement had me on the edge of my seat. I was actually on the edge of my seat throughout most of the book.<br /><br />In some parts it's really freaky and quite scary, in other parts it's sad.<br /><br />This is the second male author I've come across lately that has written female characters BETTER than the women have been writing them lately. You can't even compare Sabriel to a character like Bella. Unless you were to really dumb it down into this: Bella - sucks, Sabriel - awesome beyond all belief.<br /><br />Give this book a go. It was fun, scary, action packed and I absolutely can't wait to read the sequels!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9149832035301212414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2512814443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2512814443" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2512814443?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512814443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17842771473234001273">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <i>Death and what came after death was no great mystery to Sabriel. She just wished it was.</i>
</blockquote>Sabriel and her father have a very unique brand of magic. They can communicate with<b> the dead and the damned </b>from the Old Kingdom.<br/><br/>Only they can confront such creatures and send them<b> back to the gates of death.</b><br/><br/>Then, during the first semester of Sabriel's school, her father, the Abhorsen, goes missing and Sabriel is<b> unwittingly promoted</b> to the Abhorson.<blockquote>
  <i>Does the walker choose the path, or the path</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17842771473234001273" style="display:none">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <i>Death and what came after death was no great mystery to Sabriel. She just wished it was.</i>
</blockquote>Sabriel and her father have a very unique brand of magic. They can communicate with<b> the dead and the damned </b>from the Old Kingdom.<br /><br />Only they can confront such creatures and send them<b> back to the gates of death.</b><br /><br />Then, during the first semester of Sabriel's school, her father, the Abhorsen, goes missing and Sabriel is<b> unwittingly promoted</b> to the Abhorson.<blockquote>
  <i>Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?</i>
</blockquote>With the dead creeping ever closer to her friends and countrymen, Sabriel must go to find her father before it's too late and he transverses through<b> one gate of death too many. </b><blockquote>
  <i>Do not tarry, do not stop, no matter what happens.</i>
</blockquote><b>I've heard so many <i>wonderful </i>things about this one...that I...welll....I expected a <i>little </i>bit more...</b><br /><br />I just never felt a connection to this book - the magic, the characters, the plot -<b> all meh to me.</b><br /><br />This book relies heavily on<b> Charter Magic</b> - which, from what I can tell, involves speaking certain words and following strict rules that are <b>never fully explained</b> to the audience.<br /><br />The most frustrating part is that there's <b>no build to the magic, it's just there. </b><br /><br />It's kind of like if you jumped into the seventh Harry Potter book without the first few novels of magical background - it was <b>frustratingly complex.</b><br /><br />The other thing that really bugged me was the "love" interest.<br /><br /> Sabriel and the "love" interest<b> were essentially acquaintances </b>(or perhaps pals, if you want to stretch it) but all of a sudden, before the big battle, THIS happens: <blockquote>
  <i>"I love you," he whispered. "I hope you don't mind.</i>
</blockquote> And I'm just sitting there like, <b>
  <i>what? When did this happen?</i>
</b><br /><br />Between the magic mayhem and the bland-to-non-existent-love, <b>I never formed an emotional connection</b> to any of the main characters or the plot (other than Mogget - Mogget was the shining star in the clouded night).<br /><br />It felt like I was being <b>dragged on a journey</b> rather than eagerly plunging into a new series. <br /><br />Maybe I'll feel more connected in book 2? Anyone else feel the same?<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Tim Curry - and honestly this audio did the book NO favors. It was SO frustrating to have all these really cool concepts and absolutely NO excitement from the narrator. No tone. No characterization - other than Mogget.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17842771473234001273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <blockquote>"Yes," said Abhorsen. "I am a necromancer, but not of the common kind. where others of the art raise the dead, I lay them back to rest. And those that will not rest, I bind-or try to. I am Abhorsen . . ."<br/><br/>He looked at the baby again, and added, almost with a note of surprise, "Father of Sabriel."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Oh, what a wonderful little book. I loved Sabriel so much. She was so tough and just got things done. <br/><br/>She received a message from her fa</span>
  <span id="freeText14853081700297488353" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: $1.99 Kindle US 8/22/19</b><br /><br /> Tim Curry rocks the narration 😊💕<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"Yes," said Abhorsen. "I am a necromancer, but not of the common kind. where others of the art raise the dead, I lay them back to rest. And those that will not rest, I bind-or try to. I am Abhorsen . . ."<br /><br />He looked at the baby again, and added, almost with a note of surprise, "Father of Sabriel."</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Oh, what a wonderful little book. I loved Sabriel so much. She was so tough and just got things done. <br /><br />She received a message from her father and she knew things were not right. She wasn't sure if he was dying or what was happening at first. She received his sword and other things through a messenger. She was to be the next Abhorsen of sorts. <br /><br />This message takes Sabriel on a journey to find her father and find and kill the evil that is happening across the land. It's a bit creepy at parts which is good =) <br /><br />She has a sidekick named Mogget that she picks up at her fathers house. He's a cat and he talks and he is really something different. And he is also bound from being free. <br /><br />Then they pick up one more person that Mogget names Touchstone and he was a guard to the Queen. There's a big story there but you can read it yourself. <br /><br />They go on a journey to get away from the evil that is trying to kill Sabriel while trying to set things right. Sabriel has powers herself but she can only do so much. <br /><br />The end of the story was pretty amaze balls. I look forward to the rest of the books =)<br /><br />Happy Reading! <br /><br />Mel ❤️<br /><br />MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2018/03/sabriel-by-garth-nix.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br /><br />AMAZON: <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/review/R1BNIS2TL50EDK?ref_=glimp_1rv_cl" rel="nofollow noopener">REVIEW</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer126871115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3962824686012102284">This book really should have been exciting but I actually would have had a much better time had I just blared Monster Mash from my stereo and danced around like a zombie with chicken skin pasted to my face.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340586i/696949.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><a href='http://www.flickr.com/photos/starwarsblog/4048977628/in/set-72157622547306847/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <i>Jedi knight of the living dead!</i>
</a><br/><br/>I feel like this was probably really cool in the 90's and if I had read it then, as my pre-Harry Potter 10 year old self. I probably would have loved it. But now, my brain has descended into different forms of oblivion and I laugh voraciously at danger.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340586i/696950._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><a href='http://www.fanpop.com/spots/the-lion-king/images/12758615/title/simba-laugh-face-danger-fanart' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  </a></span>
  <span id="freeText3962824686012102284" style="display:none">This book really should have been exciting but I actually would have had a much better time had I just blared Monster Mash from my stereo and danced around like a zombie with chicken skin pasted to my face.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340586i/696949.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/starwarsblog/4048977628/in/set-72157622547306847/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <i>Jedi knight of the living dead!</i>
</a><br><br>I feel like this was probably really cool in the 90's and if I had read it then, as my pre-Harry Potter 10 year old self. I probably would have loved it. But now, my brain has descended into different forms of oblivion and I laugh voraciously at danger.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340586i/696950._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://www.fanpop.com/spots/the-lion-king/images/12758615/title/simba-laugh-face-danger-fanart" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <i>Ha-ha-haaaaa!</i>
</a><br><br>Ah shiznit - I just used a Disney movie to demonstrate how "grown up" I am. Not to mention, I said shiznit.<br><br>I'm going to give you my (bored face) half-hearted summary because the story is way to convoluted to go into much depth without lulling myself into a coma.<br><br>Sabriel is told from the third person perspective of a young girl, named Sabriel (what a co-inky-dink), a necromancer whose father disappears into the realm of the dead. She tasks herself with going to retrieve him because she believes he's still alive. Blah, blah. Monster, monster. Magic, magic.<br><br>Our heroine, Sabriel, who I probably would have thought was the kiss-ass queen of kick-ass when i was younger, seems to know exactly what to do all the time without any internal dialogue, insight, or even advice. Not to mention - training! How did she know all this stuff? Because she was destined to become the Abhorsen? Maybe that would have worked for me when I was young, naive and believed that I was going to marry Han Solo. But now, I need to see the character work and earn the right to their abilities. I need to see them struggle and angst over it like young Harry.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The overall tone of the book was chilling. And I think if I was younger, I would have been thrilled and frightened during this book but now it just didn't phase me. I wasn't even all that interested. I just felt kinda 'meh' about the whole thing.<br><br>Action scenes abound in the book; however, every single one felt completely contrived and many were repetitive. Sabriel meandered about with unclear goals and even more unclear talents. It wasn't easy to distinguish her allies from her enemies but I didn't get the impression that this was done out of poetic symbolism, merely from indistinct plotlines and story progression. I wasn't captivated by much of anything in this book. Although, I did like the cat, Mogget.<br><br>Oh, and I'm saying its slow even though I was listening to it in audio. Usually I can tolerate slower books in audio form but this one really left a lot to be desired.<br><br>The narrator was very good at distinct voices for each character but some of them, namely the monsters, were unbearable, with gasping and hissing and gurgling. He also has a teensy bit of a pretentious tone, which is understandable since he is the illustrious Tim Curry of The Rocky Horror Picture Show. But sometimes, it became annoying.<br><br>The writing was good. The world-building was good. The narration was good but I <b>never felt invested</b>. I wasn't blown away or engaged in the story or characters. I was majorly bored. And it was loooooong.<br><br>The scale of the book is huge, though. If you love sweeping epic fantasies that offer destiny as a solution to every problem with nothing to back it up (which, let's face it, is alot of fantasy), then you'd probably love this.<br><br>I really do think that this would be great for a younger audience. I think it was good, just absolutely wrong for me at this age. And if I'm being completely honest, I would much rather do the Monster Mash 100 times than go through this again.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380340586ra/696952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3962824686012102284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4612950734776347439">Very good YA fantasy! The adventures of Sabriel, an innocent young woman, and her run-ins with various types of dead, undead, once dead, sorta dead and should-be-dead people and creatures. Luckily for almost everyone concerned (except the forces of evil and the dead ones they control), Sabriel is by heritage and training a necromancer, with a fair amount of power over death. Unluckily, some of these once-dead and should-be-dead creatures have apparently killed Sabriel's father, the necromancer-i</span>
  <span id="freeText4612950734776347439" style="display:none">Very good YA fantasy! The adventures of Sabriel, an innocent young woman, and her run-ins with various types of dead, undead, once dead, sorta dead and should-be-dead people and creatures. Luckily for almost everyone concerned (except the forces of evil and the dead ones they control), Sabriel is by heritage and training a necromancer, with a fair amount of power over death. Unluckily, some of these once-dead and should-be-dead creatures have apparently killed Sabriel's father, the necromancer-in-chief or "Abhorsen," and are in the process of taking over the kingdom. It's up to Sabriel and her companions, a talking cat with mysterious powers and a once-sorta-dead (for 200 years) guy, to try to turn things around.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421038077i/13313211._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="425" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a well-written and enjoyable fantasy, occasionally a little on the grim and gruesome side, but still within the bounds of what I'd consider YA appropriate, at least for teens who aren't too sensitive. Garth Nix creates an intriguing and imaginative fantasy world. <br><br>This is also the first book in a series, but it doesn't leave you hanging off the edge of the virtual cliff. It works quite well as a stand-alone read. I haven't gotten around to reading the rest of the series, but they're on my "probably, sometime" mental list.<br><br>Content notes: Frequent battles with deadly creatures who sometimes resemble zombies. Some good characters die. The sexual content is very mild, but there's a scene where a character overhears lovemaking in the next room, and a somewhat *ahem* detailed description of a naked statue<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ who turns into an actual naked man, but that doesn't lead where you might be pardoned for thinking :)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1804028134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804028134" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804028134?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780739368251" href="/book/show/2496546.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=your-argument-is-invalid">your-argument-is-invalid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=gurrrl-power">gurrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=favorite-narrators">favorite-narrators</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804028134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12203489431691422518"><b>$1.99 on Amazon Kindle: December 21, 2017</b><br/><br/>I'll be honest: this is a book I never would have made it through unless I listened to it. TIM CURRY did a <b>
  <u>fabulous and amazing</u>
</b> job narrating this fantasy. I suppose it's "young adult," even though the book really begins with the main character being 18. Sabriel went to an all-girl school for magic. The story picks up near the end of her education. She leaves because a messenger from her father sends her his bells and sword and she realizes he is in t</span>
  <span id="freeText12203489431691422518" style="display:none"><b>$1.99 on Amazon Kindle: December 21, 2017</b><br /><br />I'll be honest: this is a book I never would have made it through unless I listened to it. TIM CURRY did a <b>
  <u>fabulous and amazing</u>
</b> job narrating this fantasy. I suppose it's "young adult," even though the book really begins with the main character being 18. Sabriel went to an all-girl school for magic. The story picks up near the end of her education. She leaves because a messenger from her father sends her his bells and sword and she realizes he is in trouble.<br /><br />Most of the story is about Sabriel's journey to save her father and escape Dead creatures and the evil free magic being called Kerrigor. Kerrigor doesn't want to stay dead and is going to destroy the world trying to reclaim Life. <br /><br />Sabriel is a necromancer, her father the greatest necromancer alive, called the Abhorsen. This is a bit "grimdark lite." There is violence, but not too many gruesome details.<br /><br />Sabriel picks up a couple sidekicks. One is another free magic creature called Mogget. As long as Mogget is bound by his collar, he looks and acts like a sarcastic small white cat. When his collar comes off, watch out! All bets are off.<br /><br />Sabriel also meets a Royal Guard named Touchstone who accompanies her on her quest. He ends up becoming a romantic interest, but it's very romance-light and nothing sappy or angsty. <br /><br />I quite liked both Mogget and Touchstone! Sabriel was a good positive female character. <br /><br />Sometimes the pacing dragged, but there were some exciting scenes as well - and GREAT world building. <br /><br />I plan to continue listening to the series, as Tim Curry narrates them all and my library has them all too! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12203489431691422518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2170342634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2170342634" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2170342634?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=supernatural-paranormal">supernatural-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2170342634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17157467319492511569"><i>“Then Sabriel hears it - the massed grinding of Dead joints, no longer joined by gristle; the padding of Dead feet, bones like hobtails clicking through necrotic flesh.” </i><br/><br/>Now, I’ll admit a book involving the dead (or zombies if you will) wouldn’t be a normal pick for me. Despite this, Sabriel kept my attention and there was plenty of magic and world building to hook me in!<br/><br/>Sabriel’s father is the Abhorsen - a necromancer with a difference! He returns the dead to their resting place, sends creature</span>
  <span id="freeText17157467319492511569" style="display:none"><i>“Then Sabriel hears it - the massed grinding of Dead joints, no longer joined by gristle; the padding of Dead feet, bones like hobtails clicking through necrotic flesh.” </i><br /><br />Now, I’ll admit a book involving the dead (or zombies if you will) wouldn’t be a normal pick for me. Despite this, Sabriel kept my attention and there was plenty of magic and world building to hook me in!<br /><br />Sabriel’s father is the Abhorsen - a necromancer with a difference! He returns the dead to their resting place, sends creatures that should be dead into death and generally protects the living from the dead!<br />When her father goes missing Sabriel must leave her boarding school, travel over the wall into the Old Kingdom and face all sorts of enemies (mainly dead or half dead or bodies taken over by dead spirits- you get the idea.) <br /><br />With delightful descriptions such as this: <br /><i>“like an apple corer punching the Dead spirit out of the rotting corpse.” </i><br /><br />The main magic system is that of Charter Magic - the use of symbols to create spells, and anyone who is a Charter Mage will have a symbol on their forehead to indicate this. It was a fantastic and creative system. <br />The other characters were great - Mogget the talking yet mysterious cat and Touchstone - the poor chap who has been trapped for 200 years and has just been rescued. <br /><br />I really enjoyed this, it was a quick read and though parts of the magic system were a bit tough to figure out I thought it was a great concept and I’ve never read anything else like it! <br /><br /><i>“Let this be my final lesson. Everyone and everything has a time to die.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="17157467319492511569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_650432534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650432534" />
    <a title="Merna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16392157-merna"><img alt="Merna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358143553p2/16392157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650432534?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merna " href="/user/show/16392157-merna">Merna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=my-2013-reads">my-2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650432534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2466370045469726570"><i>
  <blockquote>“Let this be my final lesson. Everyone and everything has a time to die.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I really wish I had liked Sabriel more than I actually did. It had a decent idea, however, as I kept reading I continuously kept thinking about events in my life or my plans for the next day. My mind kept drifting off because I was purely so bored. I believe merely saying a book is boring isn’t a convincing or a valid reason to conclude that the book wasn’t good. <br/><br/>Have you ever read a book where endless things are happen</span>
  <span id="freeText2466370045469726570" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“Let this be my final lesson. Everyone and everything has a time to die.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br>I really wish I had liked Sabriel more than I actually did. It had a decent idea, however, as I kept reading I continuously kept thinking about events in my life or my plans for the next day. My mind kept drifting off because I was purely so bored. I believe merely saying a book is boring isn’t a convincing or a valid reason to conclude that the book wasn’t good. <br><br>Have you ever read a book where endless things are happening after another, but you feel as if barely anything is occurring, because the action is always so similar to the previous ones that ensued in the book and it feels overused? <br><br>The plot essentially went like this:<br><b>Something bad happens</b><br>Sabriel defeats it<br><b>Something bad happens</b><br>Sabriel escapes<br><b>Something bad happens</b><br>Sabriel escapes<br><b>Something bad happens</b><br>Sabriel Defeats it<br><br><b>Anyway, I thought the concept for the story was intriguing at first.</b><br><br>The story is set in two fictional countries. To the south lies Ancelstierre where technology and society is comparable to the 20th century England, and to the north lies the Old Kingdom where magic and spirits wander the land. <br><br>In the Old Kingdom there is always a sorcerer with the title Abhorsen who puts the dead (spirits) to rest. The dead are raised by Necromancers or black magicians, who roam the Old Kingdom. Basically an Abhorsen is a Necromancer themselves, only they do the opposite. Sabriel is an Abhorsen who lives in Ancelstierre and her dad lives in the Old Kingdom. She sets on a journey to the Old Kingdom after her father’s sudden disappearance. <br><br><b>However, quarter way through the book:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380426695ra/852822.gif" width="390" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sabriel was a likable female character, so I have to give the male author some applause for writing believable female character. On the other hand, I felt no connection with Sabriel since her emotions where rarely expressed, instead there was a massive amount of description about many other things that caused me to yawn endlessly. Her love interest is - well, not interesting. He was flat and dull. <br><br>I feel as if I’m betraying the fantasy genre for not liking this as much as I probably should. I feel an obligation to like fantasy books that have original concepts, considering fantasy is one of my favourite genres. <br><br><b>Oh well, I still praise the idea of the story very much and I think that solely earns 3 stars, but I didn't find it to be an entertaining or engaging read for it to earn anymore than that. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2466370045469726570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1941913513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1941913513" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1941913513?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743316580" href="/book/show/21882134-sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941913513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14759892577889778760"><blockquote>#1 Sabriel ★★★☆☆<br/>#2 Lirael ???<br/>#3 Abhorsen ???<br/>#4 Clariel ???<br/>#5 Goldenhand ???</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Five Great Charters knit the land<br/>Together linked, hand in hand<br/>One in the people who wear the crown<br/>Two in the folk who keep the Dead down<br/>Three and Five became stone and mortar<br/>Four sees all in frozen water.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I first read Sabriel as a preteen, and while I know I loved it – I must have, as I asked my parents to buy me the second book in the series, too – I never continued the series, nor did I remember any of the details wh</span>
  <span id="freeText14759892577889778760" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 Sabriel ★★★☆☆<br />#2 Lirael ???<br />#3 Abhorsen ???<br />#4 Clariel ???<br />#5 Goldenhand ???</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Five Great Charters knit the land<br />Together linked, hand in hand<br />One in the people who wear the crown<br />Two in the folk who keep the Dead down<br />Three and Five became stone and mortar<br />Four sees all in frozen water.</i>
</blockquote><br />I first read Sabriel as a preteen, and while I know I loved it – I must have, as I asked my parents to buy me the second book in the series, too – I never continued the series, nor did I remember any of the details whatsoever. In recent years, I met so many people who cherish this series that I just knew I had to reread the first book, and I’m so glad that I did. While this wasn’t a perfect read for me by any means, it set the stage for what I genuinely believe is going to be an incredible series.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ necromancy ←</b><br />I’m such a sucker for necromancy books in general, and the way the world of the Dead and the Abhorsens is created in this book is wonderful, but not as fleshed out as I hoped it would be. I adored every single sentence about the world of the Dead, the bells, the magic, and the ways in which Abhorsens (Sabriel’s family of necromancers) interact with all of the above, but it was never quite <i>enough.</i> Had I gotten an extra 50-100 pages of pure, unadulterated <b>world-building,</b> I believe this would have been a 4-star read for me, if not better.<br /><br />That said, the setup we do get is magnificent: the act of necromancy is portrayed in such a fascinating and risky way, and the Dead themselves are downright creepy. These aren’t wispy ghosts and quiet whispers in shadowy halls; these are looming, vicious creatures, on a mission to regain their status among the living, no matter the cost.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Death and what came after death was no great mystery to Sabriel. She just wished it was.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Sabriel ←</b><br />The second double-edged sword in this book was Sabriel’s character, who I wanted so badly to love – and I did love, by the end – but I had <i>such</i> a hard time connecting to her! She feels very ingenuine for the first 2/3 or so of the book. Any time she feels a particularly strong emotion, it’s described to us, but in a way that feels too clinical and detached to relate to. I think this was definitely just a sign of inexperienced writing, because even by the end of the book, I was able to connect with her more solidly, and I hear that this particular writing issue is one that is resolved in the other books in this series.<br /><br />Even without feeling like Sabriel is a three-dimensional, complex character, I still soundly enjoyed who she had the potential to be. She’s tough, intelligent, and warm, without an evil bone in her body. I think the biggest reason her lack of development frustrated me was simply because, with better writing, I could have seen Sabriel becoming one of my absolute favorite heroines (and, in fact, I do remember adoring her as a child).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I love you,” he whispered. “I hope you don’t mind.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ romance ←</b><br />Finally, the reason I just could not bring myself to give this book a higher rating: <b>insta-love.</b> Funny enough, it was more of an issue with the love interest than it was with Sabriel (which, at the very least, was a refreshing change from the trope of the female in an f/m relationship being the first to fall). I won’t give any spoilers, but I will say that the quote I used at the heading of this section actually made me laugh out loud and roll my eyes a little bit. It’s not just that these two characters spend so little time together before confessing their love; it’s also a matter of the fact that they barely speak to one another throughout the entire book, as most of their limited time together is a tumultuous, stressful, and fairly quiet journey.<br /><br />On the other hand, a fellow blogger recently gave me some interesting food for thought: insta-love can be used as a plot device, to depict how naïve the characters are, and that could easily be said for the pairing in <i>Sabriel.</i> If that was the author’s intentions, I can respect it, but I still don’t feel like it was the best route; in fact, I think my preference would’ve been for this book to be entire romance-free.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You are the fifty-third Abhorsen, Sabriel. I have not taught you as well as I should – let this be my final lesson. Everyone and everything has a time to die.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ final thoughts ←</b><br />All in all, this book has a lot of flaws, but it’s got so much potential and such an interesting and unique storyline that I would ask you not to let this 3-star rating convince you for a moment that I didn’t enjoy it. On the contrary, I had a wonderful time rereading <i>Sabriel,</i> and I’ve already ordered myself a new copy of the second book so that I can see what else Garth Nix has in store for the series.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/02/17/sabriel/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!<br /><br />---<br /><br />First buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/51076954-terry-tipton" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry</a>, my love!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14759892577889778760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_50051343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50051343" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50051343?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of dark fantasy with female protagonist and horror elements</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=zombie">zombie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=father-daughter-relationship">father-daughter-relationship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=necromancy">necromancy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50051343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9542915491022157553">I shall write a wee bit about my thoughts on this book as I read, for I do not trust my foggy brain to keep up with them if I wait until the last minute.<br/><br/>*I like the juxtaposition of 20th Century (early) Ancelstierre with a medieval-esque world of the Old Kingdom. It threw me for a loop at first, how the prologue was very medieval (pre-Industrial), and the first chapter was modernesque. I was thinking, are they immortal or something? But further reading clears that up.<br/><br/>*I don't read as much pure f</span>
  <span id="freeText9542915491022157553" style="display:none">I shall write a wee bit about my thoughts on this book as I read, for I do not trust my foggy brain to keep up with them if I wait until the last minute.<br /><br />*I like the juxtaposition of 20th Century (early) Ancelstierre with a medieval-esque world of the Old Kingdom. It threw me for a loop at first, how the prologue was very medieval (pre-Industrial), and the first chapter was modernesque. I was thinking, are they immortal or something? But further reading clears that up.<br /><br />*I don't read as much pure fantasy (which I am working on changing), but this magic system stands out to me. The Charter concept. The magic system is based on sketching out these symbols that have a magical power behind them. They can also be whistled or sung, if bells are not available. <br /><br />*There are some geniuinely creepy elements that make this story borderline horrific, if not dark fantasy in tone. There were moments that held me breathless, my stomach tight with dread. I like the manner in which Nix incorporates zombies. Zombies are not a favorite horror element of mine. But this type of zombie is scary, because the emphasis is on the dark spiritual (if you will) aspects. The ability of dark Charter mages to command spirits to come back from the realms of the Dead, binding them in service. Dark stuff. The loss of free will is a big sticking point with me. Nix succeeds in unnerving me in a deeper way, and doesn't focus on the gory, squeamish aspects of zombies that repel rather than cause the fear response.<br /><br />*The author's ability to describe and propel the narrative without being too dense. I like a more natural, simplistic form of prose when I'm reading. That is what has kept me from starting some of the magic fantasy sagas, thus far.<br /><br />*The welcome elements of subtle humor. Mogget is a spirit in the form of a cat. He could not be more feline in personality. I love this scene:<br /><br /><i>Mogget had no time for such introspection, mourning or pangs of responsibility. He left her watching, blank-eyed, for no more than minute, before padding forward and delicately inserting his claws in Sabriel's slippered foot.</i>.<br /><br />That's exactly what one of my cats would do to get my attention. Haha.<br /><br />So far, I'm enjoying this read. I didn't even turn on my computer and get on Goodreads last night. I just read my book. And I turned off the tv to better concentrate.<br /><br />That's it for now...<br /><br />Update: 4/25/10<br /><br />Okay, I finished this book after 1am this morning. I loved it. It was intense, it was moving, it was written in a manner that allowed the story to flow, but with a richness of detail that made it visually stunning as I read. The magic was fascinating. Intricate, but written so that the reader doesn't feel clueless.<br /><br />I absolutely loved Sabriel. She's a strong girl. She went through such a harrowing experience. I mean, there are some truly dark moments in this story. Her father must have been so proud of her. I know I was. <br /><br />Although the book doesn't really show Sabriel with her father, (the present Abhorsen (a person who sends the restless dead back where they belong), all that much, I loved the relationship between the two. A rich father-daughter relationship always appeals in a story, and I think readers of a similar mind will enjoy this part of the book.<br /><br />For many years, I didn't read fantasy. I am sad about that, and resolved to make up for lost time. Urban fantasy and paranormal romance rekindled my childhood love of this genre. This book has truly lit me on fire to read more fantasy. I was drawn to the heroism, but also the ambiguity of this world, where the power of magic has the power to corrupt those who are not strong of mind and spirit. I'm drawn to a story where the heroine is on a journey that tests her spirit, and she comes out of it a stronger, wiser person. Sabriel definitely fits the bill for that kind of story.<br /><br />Although Sabriel is the major focus of this story, I felt that Mogget and Touchstone were strong characters that added to the texture of this story. The light romantic elements between Sabriel and Touchstone were more than welcome.<br /><br />Sabriel was a vivid, captivating, often scary introduction to the Abhorsen series, and my first read by Garth Nix. It will not be my last.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9542915491022157553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_546898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546898" />
    <a title="Heather Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47996-heather-turner"><img alt="Heather Turner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588478546p2/47996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546898?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather Turner" href="/user/show/47996-heather-turner">Heather Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060273224" href="/book/show/535197.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young Adult, Adult</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47996-heather-turner?shelf=readandloved">readandloved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16524266787495406351">Possibly one of the greatest fantasy adventures of our times, Garth Nix's first novel is a lush, magical, dark-witty adventure about a young woman's battle with the hideous Dead.<br/><br/>The story starts with a flashback in which a special necromancer named Abhorsen saves his baby daughter Sabriel from a creature called Kerrigor, in the spiritual river of death. Many years later, at an English-esque boarding school, Sabriel must take up her father's magical sword and bells and try to find out what has ha</span>
  <span id="freeText16524266787495406351" style="display:none">Possibly one of the greatest fantasy adventures of our times, Garth Nix's first novel is a lush, magical, dark-witty adventure about a young woman's battle with the hideous Dead.<br /><br />The story starts with a flashback in which a special necromancer named Abhorsen saves his baby daughter Sabriel from a creature called Kerrigor, in the spiritual river of death. Many years later, at an English-esque boarding school, Sabriel must take up her father's magical sword and bells and try to find out what has happened to him. To do so, she must leave her relatively high-tech home for the Old Kingdom, where magic rules and evil things are stalking her.<br /><br />Along the way, she is accompanied by the guard Touchstone and the menacing/funny cat-spirit Mogget. They must try to defeat the evil Kerrigor, who wants to blast the Charter which keeps all things from descending into evil.<br /><br />Sabriel is the best fantasy hero I've read about since Lord of the Rings. Too many fantasy heroines are either damsels or warrior women--Sabriel is neither. She acts and thinks precisely like a young woman in her position. Strong, intriguing, and no slack with a sword in a bad situation, she is a wonderful role model.<br /><br />Touchstone is a darling, but Mogget really is unique. Is he evil? Good? Or some peculiar mix? This ancient spirit forced to live as a cat is enslaved to the Abhorsen family for the good of everyone (we get a glimpse of how dangerous he is). The world that Garth Nix dreamed up, a mixture of Tolkien and WW2 England, is unparalleled in the fantasy genre. It's populated by animated ghouls, ghastly Mordicants, the almost-human sendings, Charter ghosts, the inhabitants of the river of Death, where only Abhorsens go, and so on...<br /><br />His writing style is lush and hypnotic--you can actually see the events unfolding in front of your eyes, in this wintry but inviting world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16524266787495406351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1410632804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410632804" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410632804?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=adventurous-acuity">adventurous-acuity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410632804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3652887146846393092">Years before I was aware of the online bookish community, the YA genre was one I was never exposed to. I read primarily classics, fantasies, and thrillers for lighter relief. One day my auntie deposited a stack of books next to me and ordered to read them all. Some of the titles included were The Hunger Games series, the Divergent series, and the first two or three books in the Abhorsen series. There were others, that I have now forgotten, but these three series are ones I can vividly recall rea</span>
  <span id="freeText3652887146846393092" style="display:none">Years before I was aware of the online bookish community, the YA genre was one I was never exposed to. I read primarily classics, fantasies, and thrillers for lighter relief. One day my auntie deposited a stack of books next to me and ordered to read them all. Some of the titles included were The Hunger Games series, the Divergent series, and the first two or three books in the Abhorsen series. There were others, that I have now forgotten, but these three series are ones I can vividly recall reading and returning to page one to reread again immediately after finishing them. I was hooked on the YA drug.<br /><br />Despite some older fantasy series, penned in the same time as this one, not standing the test of age for me, I was delighted to find that returning to this series brought me the same amount of joy as it had previously.<br /><br />Nix has constructed a fantasy world that echoes the one found in A Game of Thrones, despite perhaps a simpler version more easily accessible for younger readers. His protagonist, Sabriel, is one both fiercely independent and woefully vulnerable. The interaction between the two made her a character I immediately rooted for and empathised with. Her journey felt unique in its construction, despite following in the well-worn tread of the heroine’s journey to save the world from an imminent dark threat.<br /><br />I look forward to continuing on and discovering what more delights this series has to offer me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3652887146846393092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1958334028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958334028" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1958334028?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1958334028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7874678868526805608"><b>Sabriel is a captivating and original tale of destiny.<br/><br/><i>Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?</i></b><br/><br/>I picked up this book because Brandon Sanderson recommended it in his review for Goldenhand, the 5th book in the Abhorsen series. He termed this as "one of the fundamental experiences that helped me shape my philosophy on magic systems and worldbuilding." With such an endorsement from my favourite author of all time, I cannot possibly pass over this book. And I am glad that I didn't. <br/><br/>As </span>
  <span id="freeText7874678868526805608" style="display:none"><b>Sabriel is a captivating and original tale of destiny.<br><br><i>Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?</i></b><br><br>I picked up this book because Brandon Sanderson recommended it in his review for Goldenhand, the 5th book in the Abhorsen series. He termed this as "one of the fundamental experiences that helped me shape my philosophy on magic systems and worldbuilding." With such an endorsement from my favourite author of all time, I cannot possibly pass over this book. And I am glad that I didn't. <br><br>As a novel categorised as young adult fantasy, Sabriel is a well-crafted tale with all the necessary elements which make fantasy so enjoyable, be it for the intended target audience or more mature readers. First of all, the Prologue hooked me right from the start. It quickly establishes the notion that the titular character, Sabriel, is going to be someone special together with a glimpse of this world's magic. The narrative then jumps ahead eighteen years where Sabriel was now in the final semester of her college studies when she discovered that her father, the Abhorsen, is in mortal danger and decided immediately to head into the Old Kingdom to rescue him.<br><br>Now, let's appreciate the worldbuilding a bit. The Old Kingdom is separated from the modern world by a Wall, which keeps the Dead who wouldn't stay dead away from Ancelstierre. And if you now start to think, "Hey wait a minute, isn't that similar to ASOIAF", I would like to point out that Sabriel was published a year <i>before</i> Game of Thrones. <br><br>The modern world, Ancelstierre, is akin to our early twentieth century where there is electricity, motor vehicles and tanks, guns and ammunition. And the magic of the Old Kingdom - both in the form of Free Magic and the Charter - gets weaker the farther away one is from the Wall which demarcates the boundary between both lands. What is unusual is how the Old Kingdom appears as a completely different world. Step through the gate in the Wall, and one experiences a time and reality warp of sorts, where for one moment one is in sunny and warm Ancelstierre and then the next, in a cold and wintry landscape. Even the stars are several degrees off in the night sky, and time passes asynchronously to Ancelstierre. Its name, the Old Kingdom, also alludes to the fact that with the existence of magic, modern technology had not taken hold in this land as it did just over the Wall. <br><br>I won't go into much detail and hence spoil the fun but I will mention that the two magic systems - Free Magic and the Charter - are somewhat anathema to each other. The exposition of these two branches of magic is deftly woven into the storytelling, which avoided the dreaded info-dump. There is an aspect of music in the magic of necromancy (i.e. bells) and the Charter that I found most intriguing and, for lack of a better word, cool.<br> <br>Great worldbuilding and cool magic systems alone do not make a great fantasy book. Characters are the mortar to the bricks of good, solid storytelling. Sabriel is a great protagonist who acts her age, has her doubts, is not infallible and just feels authentic. In other words, she is not perfect, and the author does not try to make her so. Although she is quite special in her own right, the narrative does not focus on trying to hammer that fact into the reader's brains. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517727232i/24999707._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Sabriel</i><br><br>Without having much knowledge and experience required to survive the Old Kingdom in her quest to rescue her father, she has to rely on the assistance of an aloof cat, Mogget, and a young Charter Mage, Touchstone. There is always something about animal characters, whether they are capable of speech or not and this one does, that elevates the reading experience for me. In short, Mogget is superb. <br><br>If I have to pick an issue with this novel, it is the romance which felt like it came out of nowhere. Fortunately, this only appeared in small doses closer towards the end, where the book concluded most satisfactorily with an exciting page-turning climax. <br><br>For a fantasy book written before the new millennium, I take the view that it reads just as well if not better than some of its present peers - YA or otherwise. I look forward to continuing with the Abhorsen series and will recommend this to fantasy readers who are looking for well-written young female protagonists. <br><br><i>This review can also be found at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/ts-reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7874678868526805608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
