<div id="review_2426353013" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426353013" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111921-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426353013?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult">kids-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426353013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4551068352682239517">"Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?"<br/><br/>I’ve had a long-term project going for about five years now, where I try to hunt down and read all the YA adventure series that I was supposed to read when I was in middle school (instead, I spent those years re-reading the Prydain series, and also every single one of those Royal Diaries books – no regrets!). <i>Sabriel</i>, the first installment in the Abhorsen series by Garth Nix, checks off another box on that list, although I’m pretty sure t</span>
  <span id="freeText4551068352682239517" style="display:none">"Does the walker choose the path, or the path the walker?"<br /><br />I’ve had a long-term project going for about five years now, where I try to hunt down and read all the YA adventure series that I was supposed to read when I was in middle school (instead, I spent those years re-reading the Prydain series, and also every single one of those Royal Diaries books – no regrets!). <i>Sabriel</i>, the first installment in the Abhorsen series by Garth Nix, checks off another box on that list, although I’m pretty sure that I wasn’t even aware of these books until very recently. But I’m sure that they would have been right up thirteen-year-old Madeline’s alley – I can’t speak for the rest of the series, but <i>Sabriel</i> is sort of like a blend of Tamora Pierce and Lloyd Alexander, with a heavy dash of Goth elements. In short, a fun, coming-of-age adventure, featuring zombies! <br /><br />The world of <i>Sabriel</i> reminded me a little of George RR Martin’s Westeros, because we have a country (here called Ancelstierre) that’s kept separate from the Old Kingdom – a land of magic and danger. Sabriel spent the first few years of her life in the Old Kingdom with her father, a necromancer known as “the Abhorsen”, but has lived in Ancelstierre for her entire adolescence. When Sabriel is eighteen, she receives a distress message from her father. He’s trapped somewhere in Death, and Sabriel has to use the skills she learned from him to travel back to the Old Kingdom and rescue him. Along for the ride are a cat that’s not a cat, and a man who was trapped as a wooden statue for two hundred years. Oh, and evil zombies who serve an undead demon are also tracking Sabriel. <br /><br />As you can probably guess from the above description, there’s a lot of action and creepy elements in this book, as well as magic, sassy sidekicks, ghosts, and (my favorite) totally frank depictions of sexuality aimed at preteen audiences! (At one point, Sabriel considers all the implications of pursuing a sexual relationship with another character, and her mental list of Things to Deal With includes contraception! Hooray for you, Garth Nix!) Speaking of fantastic moments, I knew that Sabriel and I would get along as soon as Nix’s narration shared this tidbit with the readers: when Sabriel got her first period, she used her necromancer abilities to summon her mother’s ghost for advice. Which, frankly, why wouldn’t you? <br /><br />Even though this is part of a multiple-book series, <i>Sabriel</i> doesn’t end on a cliffhanger, and it can easily be read as a standalone novel. However, if you’re like me, you’re going to want to continue with the series, if only to find out how Sabriel continues to explore her role as a necromancer, and what other adventures Nix has planned for his heroine. <br /><br />(one more note: I listened to the audiobook version of this novel, which had two distinct advantages: first, I learned that Sabriel does <i>not</i> rhyme with “Gabriel”, like I assumed, but is pronounced “Sah-briel.” And second, the audiobook I found is narrated by Tim Curry. He’s not the best candidate for voicing an eighteen-year-old girl’s dialogue, but I didn’t even mind because his villain voices are <i>on point.</i> Voice like buttah, I’m telling you. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4551068352682239517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_33583136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33583136" />
    <a title="Judith Arvesu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/433328-judith-arvesu"><img alt="Judith Arvesu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1207686578p2/433328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33583136?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith Arvesu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith Arvesu" href="/user/show/433328-judith-arvesu">Judith Arvesu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/433328-judith-arvesu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/433328-judith-arvesu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/433328-judith-arvesu?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/433328-judith-arvesu?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33583136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6796638826142420698">When an otherworldly visitor tells Sabriel that her father has been trapped in the world of the dead, she has no choice but to leave her student's life in Ancelstierre and venture into the Old Kingdom to save him. There, in her father's absence, she must take up the mantle of Abhorsen, a necromancer charged with making sure that the dead <i>stay</i> dead. <br/><br/>Although she does not believe herself to be up to the task, Sabriel must make the journey, with only a mysterious talking cat named Mogget, and a re-</span>
  <span id="freeText6796638826142420698" style="display:none">When an otherworldly visitor tells Sabriel that her father has been trapped in the world of the dead, she has no choice but to leave her student's life in Ancelstierre and venture into the Old Kingdom to save him. There, in her father's absence, she must take up the mantle of Abhorsen, a necromancer charged with making sure that the dead <i>stay</i> dead. <br /><br />Although she does not believe herself to be up to the task, Sabriel must make the journey, with only a mysterious talking cat named Mogget, and a re-awakened amnesiac guardsman, Touchstone, by her side.<br /><br />Garth Nix is easily my favorite YA fantasy author of the moment, and one of my favorite authors full stop. Sabriel made him popular and respected among fans of the genre, and I can see why.<br /><br />It's a brilliant, fast-paced book that is quite impossible to put down. This means a lot coming from someone like me, with an average attention span of 20 pages or less. It has a solid plot, realistic characters, and a unique world built so seamlessly, it's entirely believable.<br /><br />Garth Nix is a good world builder in that he lays down the foundation of a brand-new world and lets the "fantastic" details seep through not by long-winded info-dumps but by winding them so neatly through the narrative that you hardly notice what he's doing. The world and magic of the Old Kingdom is unlike many magic systems I've come across, and it's great how he never once spends more than two pages to explain things away. Of course, this means that a number of things are left unexplored but I suppose since there are two more books in the series, there's still time to explore them there.<br /><br />His characters are also some of the most human I have ever come across. Sabriel and Touchstone are competent as heroine and hero, but are flawed enough to be interesting without ever falling into the "emo" or whiny and melodramatic pits that adolescent characters are wont to do in this genre. For all the strangeness of the world they live in, the characters are as real as can be, and the relationship between Sabriel and Touchstone develops with taste and subtlety. <br /><br />Most admirable is how Sabriel is portrayed as a normal girl with normal concerns rather than either a weeping, confused damsel or an overly masculinized (is that a word?) warrior woman. Also, she doesn't dissolve into a spineless, sex-obsessed sap when presented with a boy, despite clearly having the usual anxieties and feelings in that regard. She proves to be a quick-witted heroine, and Garth Nix doesn't cheapen her character and throws her into some really awesome, breathtaking conflicts.<br /><br />As a last note, although this is the first book of a trilogy, it's a solid story all on its own so you can pick it up with no worries as to whether you should complete the series or not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6796638826142420698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="nicklein" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein"><img alt="nicklein" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552791879p2/6058998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1794603038?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="nicklein" class="user" itemprop="url" name="nicklein" href="/user/show/6058998-nicklein">nicklein</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1794603038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6788152105487297655">Where was this book when I needed it?<br/><br/><b>5 stars!</b><br/><br/>Seriously, this book was <b>GLORIOUS</b>. If you want fast-paced, will-keep-you-on-the-edge-of-your-seat, action-packed book, this one is for you.<br/><br/>Mogget is hands down my favourite character in this book. He's so sassy and sarcastic and morbid and fluffy and I just love him!<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“It sounds like a terribly brilliant plan to me,” muttered Mogget. “The genius of simplicity…”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>The character development of Sabriel and Touchstone was brilliant especially Sabriel's. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText6788152105487297655" style="display:none">Where was this book when I needed it?<br /><br /><b>5 stars!</b><br /><br />Seriously, this book was <b>GLORIOUS</b>. If you want fast-paced, will-keep-you-on-the-edge-of-your-seat, action-packed book, this one is for you.<br /><br />Mogget is hands down my favourite character in this book. He's so sassy and sarcastic and morbid and fluffy and I just love him!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“It sounds like a terribly brilliant plan to me,” muttered Mogget. “The genius of simplicity…”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The character development of Sabriel and Touchstone was brilliant especially Sabriel's. She's totally a different person by the end of this book. And Touchstone is so dreamy. Ay kennat.<br /><br />I'm not so sure about the romance though. Don't get me wrong, you guys know I'm a sucker for romance and can ship almost every character with any living things but the romance here felt like a throwaway. It felt off. I don't know maybe it's just me. I still love our main couple though. I ship them with all my heart and wish them a fruitful relationship. Lmfao.<br /><br />The world Nix created was so complex and stunning. His descriptions were so clear that you could picture the world so vividly in your head.<br /><br />I am looking forward to read the next books in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6788152105487297655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_696507262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696507262" />
    <a title="Argona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/349639-argona"><img alt="Argona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476301474p2/349639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696507262?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Argona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Argona" href="/user/show/349639-argona">Argona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=royals">royals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=favorite-romance">favorite-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/349639-argona?shelf=zombies-undead">zombies-undead</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696507262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10508891294781691267">I have read many fantasy books and I can say with certainty that this is one of those stories that stand out. Sabriel is a very unique, interesting, complex story. Like many other fantasy books, it takes a little time to understand what is going on and really get into the story, but when that happens, you will most likely take a deep breath, dive in and refuse to come out before the end.<br/><br/>Sabriel is a young girl but she is an adult inside. A strong female character is a gem! She is not annoying or</span>
  <span id="freeText10508891294781691267" style="display:none">I have read many fantasy books and I can say with certainty that this is one of those stories that stand out. Sabriel is a very unique, interesting, complex story. Like many other fantasy books, it takes a little time to understand what is going on and really get into the story, but when that happens, you will most likely take a deep breath, dive in and refuse to come out before the end.<br /><br />Sabriel is a young girl but she is an adult inside. A strong female character is a gem! She is not annoying or dense and she understand what it means to have a responsibility.This book has great characterization. Touchstone, Maggot...all are very unique and interesting and memorable. The magic system rocks! If you like Necromancy, you have to read this.<br /><br />Is this a romantic book? Not really, this a is very intense fantasy book and romance isn't a primary element.<br /><br />Is there a very beautiful love hidden in the pages? Hell yeah! A grown up kind of love!<br /><br />In my opinion, this is a dark fantasy. Certain parts completely took my breath away. You just have to imagine and put yourself in Sabriel's place and you will successfully scare the hell out of yourselves.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading this book. I may not remember all the details after a long time but this book is unique enough that I will never confuse it with something else and I just need a few hints to remember it all.<br /><br />Are you looking for an intense, rich, fascinating fantasy book? Try this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10508891294781691267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1429228347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1429228347" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1429228347?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5602488-sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1429228347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6021195220434429051"><br/>Sabriel's father is the Abhorsen, the most powerful of necromancers who can bind the dead and stop them breaking through to the real world.Since her mother died when she was born, Sabriel is sent away to boarding school and only sees her father twice per year. The Kingdom they live in is divided into two parts with a wall protected by strong magic. Ancelstierre, the southern kingdom, where Sabriel is sent to school is safe and people live uneventful lives without the use of magic but the norther</span>
  <span id="freeText6021195220434429051" style="display:none"><br />Sabriel's father is the Abhorsen, the most powerful of necromancers who can bind the dead and stop them breaking through to the real world.Since her mother died when she was born, Sabriel is sent away to boarding school and only sees her father twice per year. The Kingdom they live in is divided into two parts with a wall protected by strong magic. Ancelstierre, the southern kingdom, where Sabriel is sent to school is safe and people live uneventful lives without the use of magic but the northern part of the kingdom, the Old Kingdom where Abhorsen must live is full of magic, good and evil where the dead can break through more easily and come back to attack the living. When Sabriel is about to leave school she receives the news that her father is dead and she must travel to the Old Kingdom to find out what has happened.<br /><br />This is a very well told YA fantasy for young and old. Sabriel is a strong female character who nevertheless makes some blunders and grows into her role. Helping her she has Mogget, a cat shaped spirit who provides some humour by making snide comments at her expense and Touchstone who becomes more likeable as the book goes on. The world building is good, with the good, safe non-magical kingdom separated from the more chaotic, magical side and the system of magic is interesting, based on an agreed Charter as well as free magic that has no rules.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6021195220434429051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2446924752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2446924752" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2446924752?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39964634-sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf-group-2018">sf-group-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2446924752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3621001226910902400">This left me very unmoved throughout. I was initially somewhat intrigued by the original depiction of the realm of the Dead, and I’m always interested in an exploration of magic interacting with dead (and undead) creatures and beings. But I would hope that a story that has so much death in it would also have some sense of the impact of death on life, and on the living, and it barely scratched that surface for me.<br/><br/>The writing is competent, the dialogue mostly flows, but the plot just feels like on</span>
  <span id="freeText3621001226910902400" style="display:none">This left me very unmoved throughout. I was initially somewhat intrigued by the original depiction of the realm of the Dead, and I’m always interested in an exploration of magic interacting with dead (and undead) creatures and beings. But I would hope that a story that has so much death in it would also have some sense of the impact of death on life, and on the living, and it barely scratched that surface for me.<br /><br />The writing is competent, the dialogue mostly flows, but the plot just feels like one incident knocking into the next, ad nauseum, with very little urgency (beyond the artificial “we only have ten minutes to do the thing we need to do!” sort of urgency) and no sense of organically connected themes and motivations. <br /><br />I understand that this book, when it was released, represented a welcome change in fantasy literature in that it features a capable, courageous, intelligent young woman as its protagonist, and I can certainly appreciate and applaud that fact. But she deserves a much richer story than what she’s given here. It was such a middle of the road reading experience for me that I won’t be continuing the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3621001226910902400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_179317052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179317052" />
    <a title="Shayantani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5686305-shayantani"><img alt="Shayantani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597354959p2/5686305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179317052?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shayantani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shayantani" href="/user/show/5686305-shayantani">Shayantani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007137312" href="/book/show/1042542.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179317052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3814150738173432">This book takes an excruciatingly long time to really pick up its pace. To be honest, if I had not bought this book about a year ago, I would definitely have quit. I have picked it up and abandoned it quite frequently over the year, mostly because about 50 pages through the book, I would start yawning. Now that is a privilege especially reserved for school textbooks, thus my reluctance. But, once you go through those first mind numbing 100 pages, this book is actually pretty decent.<br/><br/>The novel is </span>
  <span id="freeText3814150738173432" style="display:none">This book takes an excruciatingly long time to really pick up its pace. To be honest, if I had not bought this book about a year ago, I would definitely have quit. I have picked it up and abandoned it quite frequently over the year, mostly because about 50 pages through the book, I would start yawning. Now that is a privilege especially reserved for school textbooks, thus my reluctance. But, once you go through those first mind numbing 100 pages, this book is actually pretty decent.<br><br>The novel is set in two neighbouring fictional countries: The Old Kingdom to the north, where magic works and dangerous spirits roam the land and the :Ancelstierre, to the south, the “muggle land” with people blissfully ignorant except for those few who live near the border between the kingdoms. The dead refuse to stay dead, and are often raised by evil Necromancers to do their evil bidding. Here the Abhorsens comes to the rescue and puts the dead to rest. Sabriel, our protagonist, is placed with this huge responsibility of being an Abhorsen, when suddenly her father goes missing, thus, likes all fantasy heroes and heroines, she is placed with the duty of saving the world and rescuing her father. Need I mention that great adventure, life threatening dangers, amusing characters and a little romance greet her on this epic journey? <br><br>In some aspects, Sabriel definitely follows all the fantasy clichés. Yet, with a powerful plot, decent writing, loveable characters and good pacing (again, not for the first 100 pages!), I cannot bring myself to complain. The world building is amazing, with a lot of care given to minute details. The ingenious concept of death by passing through the seven gates, Saraneth and the bells, Clayrs and free magic soon made me forget about the agony of the slow start, and I found myself thoroughly enjoying the book.<br><br>So, 4 stars for the book, although I don’t reckon I would read the next part basically because, there is going to be a different set of characters, and I can’t imagine this series without Mogget.<br><br>I did mention the talking cat, right?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352055i/705573.jpg" width="220" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>MOGGET, BEST CHARACTER EVER!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3814150738173432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5095909367836968658">Possibly the greatest compliment that I could give this book is to say that it reminds me, in a non copy-cat way, of the first fantasy series to really sweep me away in my teenhood! That would be none other than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44660.The_Belgariad_Boxed_Set?from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Belgariad Series </a> by David Eddings!! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420233184ra/13193658.gif' width='245' height='156' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>Sabriel</i> is a story about a badass heroine who is charged with saving the world! <b>I love that shit, guys!!</b><br/><br/>The world building, although at times tedious, is amazing - I love the way this world is created, how death itself is portrayed AND necromanc</span>
  <span id="freeText5095909367836968658" style="display:none">Possibly the greatest compliment that I could give this book is to say that it reminds me, in a non copy-cat way, of the first fantasy series to really sweep me away in my teenhood! I love the idea of necromancers!! (Theoretically, of course) The writing, while sometimes slow, is really well done. The characters - especially Sabriel herself - are wonderfully dimensioned. The evils and dead creatures are masterfully depicted and fantastically intertwined. <b>Chris was RIGHT!! Instalove *boohiss* this romance didn't feel to me. I will note that I guessed his linage very early BUT I really don't think it's supposed to be a surprise to the reader. <div id="review_3363364524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3363364524" />
    <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance"><img alt="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600345081p2/53419883.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <a title="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance" href="/user/show/53419883-scarlett-readz-and-runz-through-novel-time-distance">Scarlett Readz and Runz....Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363364524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10469387363578441276">Wondrous storytelling ♡<br/><br/>Sabriel will be the last Abhorsen/Necromancer, but not before escaping the gates of death. <br/><br/>Born to a mother gone cold at childbirth, the Abhorsen brings the blue infant back to life and saves Sabriel as his daughter. First via wetnurse and later on at a boarding school in Ancelstierre. Sabriel is a great student and interested in the subject of Magic. Her inborn ability to reach deep within herself to rescue others from death is something she keeps hidden for as long as po</span>
  <span id="freeText10469387363578441276" style="display:none">Wondrous storytelling ♡<br /><br />Sabriel will be the last Abhorsen/Necromancer, but not before escaping the gates of death. <br /><br />Born to a mother gone cold at childbirth, the Abhorsen brings the blue infant back to life and saves Sabriel as his daughter. First via wetnurse and later on at a boarding school in Ancelstierre. Sabriel is a great student and interested in the subject of Magic. Her inborn ability to reach deep within herself to rescue others from death is something she keeps hidden for as long as possible. <br /><br />Sabriel's father visits her only annually at her boarding school and when a parcel and letter arrives instead of him one day, she realizes something terrible has happened and she must save him. <br /><br />In an amazingly imagined world that has both elements of beauty as well as darkness, Sabriel learns of the Old Kingdom and the 9 gates of death a living thing will go through to its final demise.<br /><br />As she embarks on her journey to search for her father she encounters magical creatures and makes friends and foes. While danger lurks in the Old Kingdom, she pushes on beyond more and more gates to rescue her father, presumably dead. What ensues is the dark unleash of forces from the Old Kingdom and a race against time. As the old Abhorsen puts it, <i>there is a time for everyone to die</i>, in the end, there will be only one Abhorsen left at the brink of death, but was it the right time?<br /><br />***<br /><br />This was a magical read with a most captivating beginning. If you are in search of a creative story that's very imaginative from world to creatures and love elements such as a boarding school and magic, then this will be a great one to try. <br /><br />I had this novel on my shelf for a long time and it turned out to be such a nice gem. When I can start a new book and it captures me with something different, the little extra something, it always makes me happy that I opened just that book at that time. <br /><br />Some of the imaginative elements in this novel reminded me of Neil Gaiman's writing and storytelling. If you like that sort of flavor, then you understand what I mean. It is difficult to pinpoint exactly if it's more character-driven than fantastical, it simply is a symphony of all magical, good, and evil. These perfect ingredients made Sabriel (Abhorsen,#1) a great start of a trilogy, I hope you will enjoy as well.<br /><br />Happy Reading!<br /><br />More of my reviews here:<br /><a href="https://scarlettreadzandrunz.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through Novel Time &amp; Distance</a> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10469387363578441276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1752361153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1752361153" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1752361153?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060273224" href="/book/show/535197.Sabriel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1752361153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11733012809209584531">This was a thoroughly enjoyable, fresh-feeling book about 18 year old Sabriel and her quest through the land of her birth. If more YA was written like this, I'd read more of it. Of course, I should point out that this book was published in 1995, well before the genre was Twilighted and, as such, there were no uber emo teenagers angsting over their melodramatic love triangles. And thank the universe for that! Instead we get a sensible and somewhat awkward young heroine who is afraid of the dark c</span>
  <span id="freeText11733012809209584531" style="display:none">This was a thoroughly enjoyable, fresh-feeling book about 18 year old Sabriel and her quest through the land of her birth. If more YA was written like this, I'd read more of it. Of course, I should point out that this book was published in 1995, well before the genre was Twilighted and, as such, there were no uber emo teenagers angsting over their melodramatic love triangles. And thank the universe for that! Instead we get a sensible and somewhat awkward young heroine who is afraid of the dark currents swirling around her, anxious about her abilities to meet the oncoming challenges, yet nevertheless determined to deal with any obstacles as they come. Along the way she finds help and opposition in equal measure but the focus always remains on her journey. She is young and inexperienced but she's smart enough to ask questions and to accept help when it is honestly offered - no obnoxious false bravado from this young lady.<br><br> <i>"Fear and realization of ignorance were strong medicines against stupid pride."</i><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473693317i/20502805.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story was a little slow to get moving but the writing style felt so smooth and comfortable that I didn't mind. The magic system was intriguing, as was the whole matter of dealing with the Dead, and the description of the Nine Gates painted quite a picture. It also presents a reality where a more traditional fantasy land, known as the Old Kingdom, shares a border with a more modern world - complete with cars - known as Ancelstierre. I still have some questions about how that whole situation evolved and I hope that the answers will come in the rest of the trilogy. And speaking of that, now that I know that these books are narrated by Tim Curry, I plan to finish out the trilogy in audiobook format. <br><br>P.S. I freaking LOVED Moggett!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11733012809209584531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yMDd2i57mgNR8Rwga2YJkUicN72toj6SZfS0efJnLIcMuZWRwdTtObWR1rR2RSlrzk/vhstpN/WEW7YNuYIzUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5VCsCyKIDP3k1y8Vj+UMaSqAyowjFR4TT2PU5tzn7t8hKeRAzSd7xwC35YGSxiyTrFMSt0XeF3SuzNaSlwLxCA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix">About Garth Nix</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207583754p3/8347.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix">Garth Nix

<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

11,746
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14748890993583735155">Garth Nix was born in 1963 in Melbourne, Australia, to the sound of the Salvation Army band outside playing 'Hail the Conquering Hero Comes' or possibly 'Roll Out the Barrel'. Garth left Melbourne at an early age for Canberra (the federal capital) and stayed there till he was nineteen, when he left to drive around the UK in a beat-up Austin with a boot full of books and a Silver-Reed typewriter.<br/><br/>De</span>
  <span id="freeText14748890993583735155" style="display:none">Garth Nix was born in 1963 in Melbourne, Australia, to the sound of the Salvation Army band outside playing 'Hail the Conquering Hero Comes' or possibly 'Roll Out the Barrel'. Garth left Melbourne at an early age for Canberra (the federal capital) and stayed there till he was nineteen, when he left to drive around the UK in a beat-up Austin with a boot full of books and a Silver-Reed typewriter.<br /><br />Despite a wheel literally falling off the Austin, Garth survived to return to Australia and study at the University of Canberra. After finishing his degree in 1986 he worked in a bookshop, then as a book publicist, a publisher's sales representative, and editor. Along the way he was also a part-time soldier in the Australian Army Reserve, serving in an Assault Pioneer platoon for four years. Garth left publishing to work as a public relations and marketing consultant from 1994-1997, till he became a full-time writer in 1998. He did that for a year before joining Curtis Brown Australia as a part-time literary agent in 1999. In January 2002 Garth went back to dedicated writer again, despite his belief that full-time writing explains the strange behaviour of many authors.<br /><br />He now lives in Sydney with his wife, two sons and lots of books. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14748890993583735155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
